# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

The answer includes **31 C++ source files** organized into key components:

   - Delta xDS state machine (both new and legacy versions)

   - GrpcStream template with rate limiting and retry logic
   - Abstract stream interface
   - Failover mechanism for primary/failover servers

4. **Resource Subscription Tracking**:
   - WatchMap for multiplexing multiple watches per resource type

   - UpdateAck structure
   - PausableAckQueue for ordering ACKs with pause support

6. **Supporting Infrastructure** (7 files):
   - Mux context, subscription factories, EDS resource caching, etc.

The narrative in the answer explains the complete message flow through these components: from receiving gRPC responses, validating state, delivering to interested watches, generating ACKs, and sending the next request with proper nonce acknowledgment.

We don't expect there to be new users of this class beyond\n43: //       NewGrpcMuxImpl and DeltaSubscriptionImpl (TODO(fredlas) to be renamed).\n44: //\n45: // Manages \"watches\" of xDS resources. Several xDS callers might ask for a subscription to the same\n46: // resource name \"X\". The xDS machinery must return to each their very own subscription to X.\n47: // The xDS machinery's \"watch\" concept accomplishes that, while avoiding parallel redundant xDS\n48: // requests for X. Each of those subscriptions is viewed as a \"watch\" on X, while behind the scenes\n49: // there is just a single real subscription to that resource name.\n50: //\n51: // This class maintains the watches<-->subscription mapping: it\n52: // 1) delivers updates to all interested watches, and\n53: // 2) tracks which resource names should be {added to,removed from} the subscription when the\n54: //    {first,last} watch on a resource name is {added,removed}.\n55: //\n56: // #1 is accomplished by WatchMap's implementation of the SubscriptionCallbacks interface.\n57: // This interface allows the xDS client to just throw each xDS update message it receives directly\n58: // into WatchMap::onConfigUpdate, rather than having to track the various watches' callbacks.\n59: //\n60: // The information for #2 is returned by updateWatchInterest(); the caller should use it to\n61: // update the subscription accordingly.\n62: //\n63: // A WatchMap is assumed to be dedicated to a single type_url type of resource (EDS, CDS, etc).\n64: //\n65: // The WatchMap can also store the fetched resources in a cache, and allow others to fetch\n66: // resources directly from the cache. This is done for EDS in the following case:\n67: // Assume an active EDS cluster exists with some load-assignment that is kept in the cache.\n68: // If the cluster is updated, and no load-assignment is sent from the xDS server, the\n69: // cached version will be used.\n70: // The WatchMap is responsible to update the cache with the resource contents, and it is\n71: // up to the specific xDS type subscription handler (i.e., EdsClusterImpl), to fetch\n72: // the resource from the cache.\n73: class WatchMap : public UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks, public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\n74: public:\n75:   WatchMap(const bool use_namespace_matching, const std::string& type_url,\n76:            CustomConfigValidators* config_validators, EdsResourcesCacheOptRef eds_resources_cache)\n77:       : use_namespace_matching_(use_namespace_matching), type_url_(type_url),\n78:         config_validators_(config_validators), eds_resources_cache_(eds_resources_cache) {\n79:     // If eds resources cache is provided, then the type must be ClusterLoadAssignment.\n80:     ASSERT(!eds_resources_cache_.has_value() ||\n81:            (type_url == Config::getTypeUrl<envoy::config::endpoint::v3::ClusterLoadAssignment>()));\n82:   }\n83: \n84:   // Adds 'callbacks' to the WatchMap, with every possible resource being watched.\n85:   // (Use updateWatchInterest() to narrow it down to some specific names).\n86:   // Returns the newly added watch, to be used with updateWatchInterest and removeWatch.\n87:   Watch* addWatch(SubscriptionCallbacks& callbacks, OpaqueResourceDecoder& resource_decoder);\n88: \n89:   // Updates the set of resource names that the given watch should watch.\n90:   // Returns any resource name additions/removals that are unique across all watches. That is:\n91:   // 1) if 'resources' contains X and no other watch cares about X, X will be in added_.\n92:   // 2) if 'resources' does not contain Y, and this watch was the only one that cared about Envoy always prefers fetching config from the\\n12:  * primary source, but if not available, it will fetch the config from the failover\\n13:  * source until the primary is again available.\\n14:  *\\n15:  * This class owns the state for the GrpcMux primary and failover streams, and\\n16:  * proxies the gRPC-stream functionality to either the primary or the failover config sources.\\n17:  * The failover source is optional and will only be used if given in the c'tor.\\n18:  *\\n19:  * Failover is supported in both\\n20:  * SotW (RequestType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryRequest,\\n21:  *   ResponseType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryResponse), and\\n22:  * Delta-xDS (RequestType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest,\\n23:  *   ResponseType = envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryResponse).\\n24:  * Both the primary and failover streams are either SotW or Delta-xDS.\\n25:  *\\n26:  * The use of this class will be as follows: the GrpcMux object will own an instance of\\n27:  * the GrpcMuxFailover. The GrpcMuxFailover will own 2 GrpcStreams, primary and failover.\\n28:  * Each of the primary and secondary streams will invoke GrpcStreamCallbacks\\n29:  * on their corresponding objects (also owned by the GrpcMuxFailover). both SotW (State-of-the-World) and Delta xDS modes through GrpcMuxDelta and GrpcMuxSotw specializations\\n- new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc: Unified delta-xDS-only implementation using DeltaSubscriptionState\\n- grpc_mux_impl.h/cc: Legacy implementation supporting DiscoveryRequest/Response messages\\n\\n**Protocol State Management** (Delta and SotW xDS):\\n- xds_mux/subscription_state.h: Abstract base class (BaseSubscriptionState) managing per-type_url protocol state\\n- xds_mux/delta_subscription_state.h/cc: Delta xDS state machine tracking per-resource interface for stream implementations\\n- grpc_mux_failover.h: Failover handler managing primary/failover xDS server connections with state transitions\\n\\n**Resource Watch Management**:\\n- watch_map.h/cc: Multiplexes multiple watches (subscriptions) of the same resource type, tracking interest changes and delivering updates via SubscriptionCallbacks\\n\\n**ACK/NACK Processing**:\\n- update_ack.h: Data structure for ACK/NACK messages containing nonce, type_url, and error details\\n- pausable_ack_queue.h/cc: Queue managing ACK ordering with pause/resume per type_url to handle head-of-line blocking in ADS\\n\\n**Supporting Infrastructure**:\\n- grpc_mux_context.h: Context and configuration for mux creation\\n- eds_resources_cache_impl.h/cc: Caching layer for ClusterLoadAssignment (EDS) resources\\n- xds_source_id.h/cc: Source identification for resource tracking\\n- grpc_subscription_impl.h/cc: Subscription implementation for individual resource types\\n- grpc_subscription_factory.h/cc: Factory for creating subscriptions\\n- grpc_collection_subscription_factory.h/cc: Factory for collection-based subscriptions\\n\\nThe flow: gRPC stream receives DiscoveryResponse \u2192 GrpcStream.onReceiveMessage \u2192 GrpcMux.onDiscoveryResponse \u2192 SubscriptionState.handleResponse (which validates and updates state) \u2192 WatchMap.onConfigUpdate (delivers to interested watches) \u2192 ACK generated via SubscriptionState.getNextRequestWithAck \u2192 PausableAckQueue.push \u2192 GrpcMux.trySendDiscoveryRequests \u2192 GrpcStream.sendMessage (sends DeltaDiscoveryRequest/DiscoveryRequest with nonce ACK).\"\n}\n",

multiple layers coordinating the xDS protocol:\\n\\n**Core Mux Implementations** (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/):\\n- xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc: Template-based unified mux supporting both SotW (State-of-the-World) and Delta xDS modes through GrpcMuxDelta and GrpcMuxSotw specializations\\n- new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc: Unified delta-xDS-only implementation using DeltaSubscriptionState\\n- grpc_mux_impl.h/cc: Legacy implementation supporting DiscoveryRequest/Response messages\\n\\n**Protocol State Management** (Delta and SotW xDS):\\n- xds_mux/subscription_state.h: Abstract base class (BaseSubscriptionState) managing per-type_url protocol state\\n- xds_mux/delta_subscription_state.h/cc: Delta xDS state machine tracking per-resource versions, resource subscriptions, and state transitions\\n- xds_mux/sotw_subscription_state.h/cc: State-of-the-World xDS state machine tracking version_info and requested resources\\n- delta_subscription_state.h/cc: Legacy delta subscription implementation\\n\\n**gRPC Stream Communication** (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/):\\n- grpc_stream.h: Template-based GrpcStream<RequestProto, ResponseProto> implementing rate limiting, backoff retry logic, and stream lifecycle (establishNewStream, sendMessage, onReceiveMessage)\\n- grpc_stream_interface.h: Abstract interface for stream implementations\\n- grpc_mux_failover.h: Failover handler managing primary/failover xDS server connections with state transitions\\n\\n**Resource Watch Management**:\\n- watch_map.h/cc: Multiplexes multiple watches (subscriptions) of the same resource type, tracking interest changes and delivering updates via SubscriptionCallbacks\\n\\n**ACK/NACK Processing**:\\n- update_ack.h: Data structure for ACK/NACK messages containing nonce, type_url, and error details\\n- pausable_ack_queue.h/cc: Queue managing ACK ordering with pause/resume per type_url to handle head-of-line blocking in ADS\\n\\n**Supporting Infrastructure**:\\n- grpc_mux_context.h: Context and configuration for mux creation\\n- eds_resources_cache_impl.h/cc: Caching layer for ClusterLoadAssignment (EDS) resources\\n- xds_source_id.h/cc: Source identification for resource tracking\\n- grpc_subscription_impl.h/cc: Subscription implementation for individual resource types\\n- grpc_subscription_factory.h/cc: Factory for creating subscriptions\\n- grpc_collection_subscription_factory.h/cc: Factory for collection-based subscriptions\\n\\nThe flow: gRPC stream receives DiscoveryResponse \u2192 GrpcStream.onReceiveMessage \u2192 GrpcMux.onDiscoveryResponse \u2192 SubscriptionState.handleResponse (which validates and updates state) \u2192 WatchMap.onConfigUpdate (delivers to interested watches) \u2192 ACK generated via SubscriptionState.getNextRequestWithAck \u2192 PausableAckQueue.push \u2192 GrpcMux.trySendDiscoveryRequests \u2192 GrpcStream.sendMessage (sends DeltaDiscoveryRequest/DiscoveryRequest with nonce ACK).\"\n}\n",
